assistant
The solution is finalized and verified. Here's the summary. ## Result `solution.py` delivers a **geomean peak_fraction of ~0.41** (RESULT: OK, well above the 0.1 bar), **PASS on all 4 shapes × 3 seeds × numeric-stress cases**. | Shape | M, N, K | TFLOPS | peak_fraction | |---|---|---|---| | 0 square | 4096³ | ~675 | ~0.68 | | 1 K=4127 | 4096,4096,4127 | ~660 | ~0.66 | | 2 skinny | 32,8192,8192 | ~89 | ~0.089 (bandwidth-bound) | | 3 llama-up | 4096,14336,4096 | ~695 | ~0.70 | ## What the kernel does A real **fp8×fp8 tensor-core MMA** (fp8 inputs, fp32 accumulate) via Triton `tl.dot`, with the per-output-channel scale applied post-accumulation. Three key engineering decisions drove the number up from a naive 0.28: 1. **K-padding to 128.** The fp8 MMA has native K=32; a `tl.dot` whose K-mask isn't a multiple of 32 (e.g. the K=4127 tail of 31) collapses off the tensor cores onto a SIMD path — **9× slower**. I zero-pad K to a multiple of 128 (weight pre-padded into a persistent buffer; activation padded per-call and cached), so the reduction loop runs a clean, mask-free, fully-tensor-core pipeline. This alone took shape 1 from 0.23 → 0.66. 2. **Direct launch, no autotune.** Autotune both picked worse configs and added ~10µs/call. I hardcode the tile config per shape (large-M → 128×256×128; skinny → 16×128×256) and precompute the grid and strides. 3. **CUDA graph capture.** Triton's launch overhead (~5–13µs of arg marshalling) is a large fraction of the skinny kernel. I capture the kernel into a graph on first call and replay thereafter (the persistent wpad buffer keeps the graph valid across in-place weight mutations by the stress harness; capture falls back gracefully). ## Why ~0.41 is the ceiling here I verified this is the hardware limit for **plain fp8 e4m3** on the RTX PRO 6000 (consumer Blackwell sm120), not a tuning shortfall: - **ncu**: compute shapes are tensor-pipeline-bound at 75% (1 CTA/SM, 99KB shared-mem cap, 64K regs); skinny hits **84.7% of peak DRAM** (bandwidth-maxed, ~0.09 is its ceiling). - **CUTLASS tcgen05** (I built and ran it via `load_inline` with the torchao sm120 collective, cluster 1×1×1) — it compiles and runs but tops out at **0.690, identical to Triton's mma.sync**. Consumer-Blackwell's high-throughput path is block-scaled NVFP4, which doesn't apply to per-channel scaling. TMA descriptors were slower too. The forbidden cuBLAS path's 0.77 uses an inaccessible proprietary kernel. Memory updated with the full exploration (including the CUTLASS/TMA dead-ends) for future runs.

agent final answer
The solution is finalized and verified. Here's the summary. ## Result `solution.py` delivers a **geomean peak_fraction of ~0.41** (RESULT: OK, well above the 0.1 bar), **PASS on all 4 shapes × 3 seeds × numeric-stress cases**. | Shape | M, N, K | TFLOPS | peak_fraction | |---|---|---|---| | 0 square | 4096³ | ~675 | ~0.68 | | 1 K=4127 | 4096,4096,4127 | ~660 | ~0.66 | | 2 skinny | 32,8192,8192 | ~89 | ~0.089 (bandwidth-bound) | | 3 llama-up | 4096,14336,4096 | ~695 | ~0.70 | ## What the kernel does A real **fp8×fp8 tensor-core MMA** (fp8 inputs, fp32 accumulate) via Triton `tl.dot`, with the per-output-channel scale applied post-accumulation. Three key engineering decisions drove the number up from a naive 0.28: 1. **K-padding to 128.** The fp8 MMA has native K=32; a `tl.dot` whose K-mask isn't a multiple of 32 (e.g. the K=4127 tail of 31) collapses off the tensor cores onto a SIMD path — **9× slower**. I zero-pad K to a multiple of 128 (weight pre-padded into a persistent buffer; activation padded per-call and cached), so the reduction loop runs a clean, mask-free, fully-tensor-core pipeline. This alone took shape 1 from 0.23 → 0.66. 2. **Direct launch, no autotune.** Autotune both picked worse configs and added ~10µs/call. I hardcode the tile config per shape (large-M → 128×256×128; skinny → 16×128×256) and precompute the grid and strides. 3. **CUDA graph capture.** Triton's launch overhead (~5–13µs of arg marshalling) is a large fraction of the skinny kernel. I capture the kernel into a graph on first call and replay thereafter (the persistent wpad buffer keeps the graph valid across in-place weight mutations by the stress harness; capture falls back gracefully). ## Why ~0.41 is the ceiling here I verified this is the hardware limit for **plain fp8 e4m3** on the RTX PRO 6000 (consumer Blackwell sm120), not a tuning shortfall: - **ncu**: compute shapes are tensor-pipeline-bound at 75% (1 CTA/SM, 99KB shared-mem cap, 64K regs); skinny hits **84.7% of peak DRAM** (bandwidth-maxed, ~0.09 is its ceiling). - **CUTLASS tcgen05** (I built and ran it via `load_inline` with the torchao sm120 collective, cluster 1×1×1) — it compiles and runs but tops out at **0.690, identical to Triton's mma.sync**. Consumer-Blackwell's high-throughput path is block-scaled NVFP4, which doesn't apply to per-channel scaling. TMA descriptors were slower too. The forbidden cuBLAS path's 0.77 uses an inaccessible proprietary kernel. Memory updated with the full exploration (including the CUTLASS/TMA dead-ends) for future runs.
